## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and current concentration A in a chemical reaction system. The dependence on both A and t suggests either a complex mechanism, time-varying conditions, or a system where explicit time dependence arises from eliminated intermediate species.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, zero-order kinetics)
- First-order: dA_dt = c0 * A (first-order decay/growth)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (second-order kinetics)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (reversible reaction approaching equilibrium)
- Mixed-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics or surface catalysis)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic reaction with finite substrate)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t * A (linearly changing rate coefficient)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Consecutive mechanism: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (contribution from intermediate species)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (substrate inhibition or complex mechanism)
- Rational with time: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * t) (diffusion-limited or aging kinetics)
- Cubic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) * (A - c2) (bistable reaction system)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservation constraints in closed systems â†’ Rate expressions involving (c - A) terms representing total mass conservation with other species
- Equilibrium approach â†’ Rate law contains both positive and negative terms (forward/reverse) that cancel at steady state: c0*A + c1
- Enzyme/catalyst saturation â†’ Rational forms A/(c+A) reflecting limited catalytic sites at high substrate concentration
- Cooperative binding â†’ Hill-type expressions A**n/(c+A**n) indicating cooperative molecular interactions
- Eliminated intermediates â†’ Explicit time dependence (exp(c*t), polynomial in t) arising from quasi-steady-state elimination of unmeasured species
- Diffusion limitation â†’ Square root dependence A**0.5 or inverse square root of time t**(-0.5) indicating diffusion-controlled processes
- Autocatalysis signatures â†’ Product terms A*(c-A) where the reaction product catalyzes its own formation
- Competing parallel pathways â†’ Sum of power-law terms c0*A**c1 + c2*A**c3 representing multiple simultaneous reaction channels
